Public Announcement of Memorial Service for Wu Jian'an 160

Wu Jian'an, a lawyer and member of the Shanghai Wu County Lawyers Association, was a kind and benevolent person. Most of his income was spent on purchasing various medicines for common illnesses and distributing them, which was admired by his peers. He did this for several years. This New Year, he suddenly suffered from a deficiency of qi and blood and passed away on Lichun. Colleagues in the legal profession felt that Mr. Wu's situation was bleak, so it was decided to hold a memorial service at the Jiangping Public Office on the 22nd of February. Yesterday, a public announcement for the memorial service was issued, stating: "Dear Sir/Madam, Wu Jian'an's family was of Confucian tradition. He lost his father in his childhood and was raised by his mother, Madam Wang, who maintained her chastity. He studied and became successful. In the early years of the Republic of China, he worked in the law firm of Ze Min for a long time. After Ze Min went north to take a seat in Parliament, Wu was hired by Yi Peng for nearly ten years. During this time, he also served as a clerk for the Shanghai Lawyers Association for several years. Before the reorganization of the Association, the reports were all written by him. Recently, he joined the Shanghai Wu County Lawyers Association and performed his duties. His character, learning, and experience were rare among his peers. Over many years, he compiled two volumes of Explanations of the Supreme Court, which continued the tradition of official books and became a great work, benefiting the legal profession and highly regarded in the country. Unfortunately, he had a history of asthma, and also because of excessive exertion, he suffered from a deficiency of qi and blood and passed away in the spring at the young age of forty-seven. He was buried in a coffin, and his family was impoverished. His elderly mother was in great pain and wanted to die, and his wife and children were unable to survive. Their cries were the most tragic scene in life. Among his surviving children, besides the eldest who is already married, there are still two sons and two daughters whose studies and marriages will be a great difficulty in the future. We, his colleagues, feel heartache and cannot but do our best to help each other. We have chosen to hold a memorial service at the Xin Zha Pingjiang Public Office at 2 p.m. on February 22 to commemorate him. We respectfully request that all wise men in the country and colleagues in the legal profession generously donate money so that his family can rely on it and both the living and the dead will be grateful. We respectfully inform you of our humble request. Zhang Yi'ao, Chen Fumin, Lu Bohong, Zhu Shoucheng, Wang Caiyun, Fan Huichun, Zhang Yipeng, Cai Nipei, Tan Yigong, Zhang Jiazhen, Zhang Zongru, Chen Zemin, Zhao Zuwei, Liu Zuwang, Huang Huansheng, Jiang Yiping, and 30 others jointly announce."

Songhu Rehabilitation Institute Plans to Build Factory 161

The Songhu Rehabilitation Institute covers an area of more than one hundred acres. In addition to the construction of the institute's buildings, the eastern end has a spacious area with a mountain and a deep pool that doesn't dry up. Whoever climbs the mountain and looks out gets a refreshing feeling. Last year, after Director Wang Zhaocheng took office, he visited the institute every day to supervise. He was deeply saddened that the eastern wasteland was abandoned and uncultivated. He reported to the Social Affairs Bureau and was approved to cultivate the land and plant vegetables for food. Now, the number of unemployed vagrants in Shanghai is increasing, and it is impossible to accommodate them all. The institute is already full and cannot accommodate any more. It is now planned to add new buildings and expand the factory in the hope of accommodating more people and stabilizing society. The construction funds are planned to be raised from wealthy businessmen in Shanghai. If it is not enough, other methods will be found. The factory will advertise for investment and open various factories so that the institute's residents can learn skills and support themselves after leaving the institute. The factory site will be provided by the institute.

Small Fire in Pig Alley 166

Yan Jusheng from Ningbo, who lives in house No. 74 in Pig Alley outside the South Gate of the South City. The house has two upper and two lower floors. Yan lives on the upper floor of the living room, and the side room on the upper floor is rented to the Xie Shi family from Huzhou. The wing room floor is rented to his fellow villager Sun Kangde. At approximately 5 a.m. yesterday morning, the house suddenly caught fire and quickly became a disaster, bursting through the roof. The Fire United Association immediately sounded the alarm. Soon, fire engines from various fire brigades arrived at the scene and connected water to extinguish the fire. It took about half an hour to extinguish. The side room on the upper floor of the living room and the back building were burned down. When the fire was raging, Yao Jinkui, the watchman of the 12th Squad, took Yan Jusheng, Sun Kangde, Xie Shi, etc., back to the Third Precinct of the First District for preliminary examination before the chief examines the case.

History of Tobacco and Alcohol Tax Published 170

Tobacco and alcohol tax is a major source of income for our country. Since the establishment of the special tax in the Qing Dynasty, it has been a long time, and there have been many changes and benefits during this period. However, there are no specialized writings on this subject in both public and private sectors, which is regrettable for those concerned about tax administration. Last year, the Tobacco and Alcohol Tax Department of the Ministry of Finance specially established a Tobacco and Alcohol Tax Affairs Committee to start editing the History of Tobacco and Alcohol Tax. The content is divided into ten chapters: evolution, region, tax system, public sales fees, tobacco and alcohol tax, license tax, cigarette tax, foreign liquor tax, overview of revenue and expenditure, and overview of sorting out. Relevant public and private writings on tobacco and alcohol tax are attached at the end for reference. The authors of this book are all well-known figures with knowledge and experience. The descriptions of tax rule changes and the current system are very detailed. It is a great work in the financial world. The upper volume has been published and is sold by the Dadong Bookstore in this city. The lower volume is being proofread and will be published soon.

Zhong Ling Printing Machine Sold to the United States 171

A Chinese merchant from the United States, Mr. Li Junyao, purchased ten Zhong Ling air pressure machines from the Hanli Company and shipped them to the United States. The overseas Chinese merchants believe that the machine is easy to print and can be called the world's supreme victory, which is enough to resist mimeograph machines. They were sold out quickly, and each machine was sold for 60 US dollars. Although the US import tax is expensive, there is still a large profit to be made. It is now heard that Mr. Li has telegraphed the Baoling Company in Hong Kong to contact the Shanghai Hanli Company to negotiate the general agency in the United States and to guarantee the sale of 160,000 yuan per year. Both parties have agreed on a contract. Our country's new manufactured products are sold in the most developed countries in manufacturing, and this should be the first.

Correspondence 173

To whom it may concern, our hospital has always followed the Health Bureau's guidelines for smallpox vaccinations. We have checked and found that from January to February 19th of the nineteenth year, no smallpox patients came to our hospital for treatment. The information published in your newspaper yesterday was likely based on inaccurate rumors. We are writing this letter to clarify the matter and request that it be published in the "Letters to the Editor" section to ensure accuracy. Sincerely, Wang Zhen, Shanghai Pudong Hospital, to the Editorial Department of Shen Bao.

Esteemed Editor, I am writing to you regarding the news item under the headline "Husband and Wife Incompatible" in today's local news section of your newspaper, which concerns me and has caused me great alarm upon reading it. The truth is, I married a woman named Chen, but due to her inability to please my elders, domestic disputes arose from time to time. In order to seek peace, I personally sent her to live with her mother in the autumn of the seventeenth year and provided her with monthly alimony. For over ten months, this arrangement caused no issues. However, near the end of the lunar year of last year, I received a summons from the First Precinct of the First District, ordering me to go to the station. I then learned that she had come to Shanghai and, at the instigation of others, intended to make trouble for me. I explained the circumstances of my family to the precinct chief, who, after understanding the situation, instructed both parties to reconcile outside the station. However, reconciliation could not be achieved because her demands were excessive and I was unable to meet them. On my part, I have always hoped that she would reform and reconcile, and I have adopted a policy of waiting and seeing how things develop. I believe that she would not dare to take any extreme actions. The report in yesterday's newspaper about a mutual scuffle is entirely fabricated. I respectfully request that your esteemed editor provide a correction to avoid misleading the public. I would be most grateful. Respectfully submitted, Mi Chuxin, No. 3 Hexing Lane, Wangjia Wharf, South City, February 19, 19--.

Free Talk

Farewell to the Gentlemen of the National Walking Tour 178

— Shou Juan

In my youth, I read English books such as *Robinson Crusoe* and Mr. Liang Rengong's *Fifteen Young Heroes,* which often sparked my imagination.

I wanted to emulate Robinson Crusoe and drift to a deserted island, and I also wanted to follow the fifteen young heroes and explore the wilderness. At that time, my ambition soared to the sky and I was truly invincible. But as time went by, my age increased year by year, and my family burdens became heavier and heavier. My ambition also decreased year by year. Living in this beautiful and prosperous Shanghai for a long time, I have been completely corrupted. I have neither finished reading ten thousand books nor do I want to walk ten thousand miles. Recently, I heard that Mr. Xie Fensheng, Ge Wenlie, Liu Hanqiao, Lou Xia, Zhuang Xueben, Xu Yintang, Xu Zengxiang, Liang Daxin, Jiang Xixi, and others have organized a national walking tour that will traverse the entire country in five years, without turning back despite all difficulties. Such a great undertaking is truly unprecedented. I cannot help but feel my heart flutter and regret that I cannot get rid of everything and go with them. The night before last, at the farewell banquet, I personally heard the great theories of these gentlemen and learned that their organization is very complete and their ambitions are very great. This trip will investigate the history, geography, local customs, languages, literature, economy, industry, education, transportation, and other conditions of various places, and collect evidence to provide society with academic and construction references. They are prepared to fight against any difficulties and dangers with the blood and sweat of nine people, hoping to achieve the final victory and return fully loaded. This fearless spirit of the new China and the new youth is worthy of our advocacy and worship. Today is the day of departure for these gentlemen. I dare to offer a heartfelt blessing for their health and success.

News about the 300th Anniversary of Wu Meicun 179

— Jun Shuo

Recently, our country's scholars have focused their minds on science, which has inevitably led to the gradual decline of traditional Chinese studies. However, many countries in Europe and the West have turned to embracing our country's traditional Chinese scholars, especially France. It is said that many of the four major books in our country have been translated. Recently, I heard from a certain doctor who returned from Paris that the French especially admire Mr. Wu Meicun of Taicang among our country's literary figures. They have already made a very solemn expression, saying that one day they will form a group and come to China to visit Mr. Ke Li and hold a 300th anniversary memorial meeting. Their worship has reached its peak. If it becomes a reality, it will be an unprecedented grand event. Now, according to the genealogy of Mr. Wu Meicun written by Gu Shishi of Taicang, he was born on May 20th of the 37th year of the Wanli period of the Ming Dynasty and died on December 24th of the 10th year of the Kangxi period of the Qing Dynasty. From the 11th year of the Kangxi period to the 19th year of the Republic of China, it has been 259 years. The date of the 300th anniversary memorial is still 41 years away. When the meeting is held, I am afraid that those who initiated this proposal may not all be able to witness its grandeur in person. It is impossible not to hope that those who come later will inherit the previous aspirations. Wu Yuyang's poem says, "White hair filling in the words of the wine sacrifice of Wu." Yuan Zicai's poem says, "Born in the turbulent years of Tianbao, marvelously chanting the long celebration chapter of Xiangshan. Even if the hearts of the Wu people are wooden and stone, they should also read it and be moved." Its value can be known. Mr. name is Weiye, Zi Jungong, and Meicun is his other name. He became the champion in the provincial examination at the age of twenty-three. In the imperial examination, he was ranked second in the first class, the second scholar, and entered the Hanlin Academy. The edict said, "Lu Ji's poems and essays were unique in Jiangdong in his early years. Su Shi's articles spread throughout the capital in one day." At that time, it was considered not to be unworthy. As for his entry into the Qing Dynasty, he served as the libationer, recommended by the two prime ministers of Liyang Hai Ning and the governor Ma Guozhu. However, the officials at that time were urgent and forced him to take office. The two parents shed tears, and they feared that resisting the imperial decree would lead to unforeseen consequences. Mr. wrote a poem to Governor Ma, saying, "Ashamed to be recommended as a virtuous minister by Xiao Xiangguo, Zhao Ping is only fit to guard the melon hill." He also sighed and said, "Wasted a lifetime in officialdom. It is easy to abandon the family but difficult to change the name." However, his deathbed words were, "It is not easy to abandon wife and children, but what is the use of saying that it is not worth a penny." Mr. left because he could not bear to burden his parents, but he said that he missed his wife and children, and his intentions can be said to be extremely bitter. Now, foreigners still admire him. Not only is his writing more prominent, but his heart is also greatly understood.

A Description of the Newly Invented Artificial Rain Ball 180

— Ji Jin

My friend, Mr. Xu, has studied in France for many years and specialized in mechanics. According to a recent newsletter, the French are naturally fond of danger. They spare no effort in their intelligence to engage in earth-shattering undertakings. The Mont Cenis Tunnel, the Suez Canal, and the Panama Canal are especially large examples. Recently, in view of the Sahara Desert in non-French Africa, which spans more than three thousand miles, where the soil is dry and it does not rain all year round, which is a major obstacle to colonization, after repeated research by scholars, Professor Lorte of the Science Department of Gesnai Duang University invented the latest artificial rain ball. The method is to first put a kind of coldest gas into a rubber ball, and tie it with a button at the lower end. Then use electricity to transport it and let it rise into the air. After a long time, the ball gradually breaks due to the rotation of the button. The gas then comes out through the cracks and spreads throughout the air like clouds. It suddenly reduces the heat generated by the sun in the upper layer. At this time, the sparse heat in the air mixes with the heavy cold air in the ball, forming extremely fine water droplets that fall gently. Although the momentum is not great, it is enough to nourish the millet seedlings and moisten the soil.

Last winter, Lorte personally went to the Sahara to test the ball. He opened the ball from 10:00 AM to 11:00 AM. It looked like a hazy mist, but the two spots did not fall. He then added enough power and radiated it directly into the air. It was not until after 1:00 PM that dark clouds gathered and the sky was dark. It rained heavily, and everything within a mile was soaked. This was the first test. Later, he conducted second and third tests in Vistre, a nearby place, and the efficiency was more obvious. The raindrops were fine, dense, and even, and could spread to four or five miles away. Lorte was very happy, believing that within ten years, this vast and boundless wasteland could be transformed into a fertile area for utilization and enrichment. It can be determined that more forests must be planted, then the weather and geology will change. The Egyptian desert, which used to rain once a year, now rains once a season. In the future, it may rain once a month. With the evolution of the world's material civilization, how can we see that the power of science is not enough to seize the work of creation?

On Hobbies 181

— Chun Hua

Almost everyone has special hobbies. Using a person's hobbies to determine their personality is the most accurate test. I am a mediocre person. My life has been uneventful. But my hobbies are worth mentioning. In terms of food, I like salty and sour flavors and hate sweet flavors. When I read books, I liked to read clever and witty essays and hated lofty and classic books. In recent years, I have been very fond of watching movies. Among Western stars, I like Janet Gaynor the most. The famous films she starred in, such as *Seventh Heaven*, *Sunrise*, *Street Angel*, and *Four Devils*, have deeply moved me. Her technique is not the highest, but I don't know why, the power of her inspiration to me is extremely great. As for stage plays, I was very fond of Cheng Yanqiu in Beijing for several years. In recent years, I have been working at night in Shanghai, and I have very few opportunities to watch plays. When Cheng comes, I can only watch him once on Sunday. Among the records, I like listening to Xun Huisheng's records the most. Huisheng's singing deeply grasps the essence of writing, lingering and exquisite. The records recorded by other actors have many tasteless tastes. Furthermore, when it comes to reading newspapers, I always ignore military and national affairs and browse social news. I can read almost every word without missing one. There are many strange things in Shanghai society. The newspaper only selects a small part of them. I feel that I have had enough of it. Also, in the past, I was addicted to playing mahjong. I did not listen to any warnings. I even wrote to praise the game, believing that the construction and configuration of mahjong have mathematical interest and are in line with aesthetics and mechanics. The choice of taking or discarding cards is also full of psychological research. It is also meticulous and without flaws. It can be called the saint of gambling in the world. In recent years, I have seen a little more of the world, and my love for it has faded. But I have become even more fond of Go. I believe that I am the most uncontrollable and mediocre person.

The Romantic Fortune of a Defrocked Monk 183

— Yu'an

There is a tobacco and paper shop on Datong Road, established by a defrocked monk. It has now changed hands. The monk's surname is Luo, and he is from Yancheng.

While still a monk, he was the abbot of a certain temple. The temple was quite wealthy. Within a few years, Luo accumulated assets of four or five thousand yuan. His six senses were not yet cleansed, and he had an affair with a woman in the vicinity. They were secretly carrying on, not just occasionally. The woman had a husband, who eventually found out about the affair. He was furious. Instead of blaming his wife, he planned to hire thugs to beat up Luo. The woman secretly told Luo about the plan. Luo was afraid. Relying on his savings, he resolutely removed his cassock and urged the woman to elope with him. They then came to Shanghai together. After living there for half a year, he opened this tobacco and paper shop. The woman's husband also managed to find out their whereabouts. He wanted to take revenge. Coincidentally, Yancheng was experiencing a famine, and life was difficult. So, he brought his mother and younger sister to Shanghai. He planned to find work, and have his mother and sister work as servants. He also intended to reclaim his wife.

The day after arriving in Shanghai, he and his sister went to spy on Luo. As expected, they saw Luo, but he had changed into secular clothes. They did not see the woman. Not daring to act, Luo was at the counter doing business. Suddenly, he noticed two people lingering. Upon closer inspection, he recognized his enemy. He was greatly alarmed and went inside to tell the woman. The woman immediately escaped through the back door and hid in the neighbor's house. Her husband and sister watched for three days, but never saw the woman. They were at a loss. They instructed the sister to come and check from time to time, while the husband went to find work. After more than ten days, the woman's guard was slightly lowered. She happened to be standing in front of the door when the sister saw her. Delighted, she approached the woman. The woman was flustered. Seeing that only the sister was present, and not her husband, she was not afraid. She quickly invited the sister into the room and they talked about what had happened since they had last met. The woman boasted about Luo's wealth. The sister was quite envious. She was already over twenty and still had no husband. Before the woman had eloped, the sisters-in-law had gotten along well. Moreover, the woman had never given birth. Luo, now a layman, was very concerned about having descendants. The woman worried that she might be abandoned in the future. Luo might marry someone else, and she would inevitably be discarded. She also thought that her sister was meek and would not threaten her position. So, she used her eloquent tongue to persuade her to follow Luo. The sister agreed. Thus, Luo killed two birds with one stone, and was completely satisfied. He then sold his shop and still had several thousand gold coins. He took the woman and her sister and left to avoid trouble for a while. Although they were still in Shanghai, the woman's husband could no longer find them. He could not reclaim his wife, and he had lost his sister. He was extremely frustrated. When his mother arrived, she broke down and cried in front of the shop. People in the area then learned the whole story. Many condemned Luo and felt sorry for the woman's husband.

Warmth in the Heart (132) 184

— Bao Tianxiao

Chapter 9: Notables Uproariously Play Hide-and-Seek, a Charming Woman Willfully Gives Protection

Let's talk about the spring farewell party on March 30th. It was Zuo Shichen's turn to be on duty. That evening, he hosted a banquet at the Mingjing Club. At this time, the weather was gradually getting warmer. Shanghai's commercial affairs are densely populated, and the houses are lined up one after another. It is often difficult to find an open space. However, this racetrack is in the center of the concession, the most prosperous and lively place, but this open and sparse grassland is left behind. It is truly rare and valuable. That night, because the weather was warm, the windows facing the racetrack were opened, and the gentle breeze flowed in, blowing on the face without feeling cold. The girls were all wearing light cotton clothes. At this time, camel wool had not yet prevailed in China. When the spring cold was still tight, everyone wore silver fox and pearl skin clothes. Removing the small fur clothes, they wore cotton clothes. Those who were particular used fine needles and dense threads to sew them, calling them ten-thread cotton jackets. A group of tailors came up with new patterns, using silk threads to sew various patterns, such as plum blossoms on broken branches, or large orchid flowers, or flowers, bamboo, mountains and rocks, or feathered figures. In short, you like that look, you can sew that look. What you can say can be done. Today's Su Jun wore a West Lake-colored ten-thread cotton jacket made of Huzhou crepe, with apricot blossoms and swallows sewn on it. The Yiqing Xianguan wore an襖zi made of water-gray patterned black velvet. That kind of velvet, although said to be produced in Zhangzhou, Fujian, has recently been woven by weavers in the Nanjing area. Wearing it is enough to make people look at her. The other girls were also competing for beauty. Only Hua Ruiyun wore a cotton jacket made of shimmering flower satin inside. It is said that the clothes were not her own, but her older sister Hua Ruiyun's first. She inherited her older sister's name, but she was Hua Ruiyun the second. Her older sister was the first adopted daughter of the old madam and was also a famous prostitute. She was married off the year before, and the old madam made a lot of money. So, now she is teaching her to inherit this brand, hoping that her business and her fame will not be less than her older sister. Secondly, with this winning brand, it cannot but continue to be used. The brands of the leading girls in the hall, like the famous trademarks in the business world, are equally valuable. After the old madam married off Hua Ruiyun the first, there were still many clothes hidden in the boxes. Now, take them out and see that there are many clothes that have only been worn two or three times and folded in the boxes. It is really a pity to tear them down and remake them. However, no matter what era, women's decorations and clothes change the fastest. Because silk and satin shops and garment makers are thinking about turning over new patterns all day long. If a style is set down and never changes, and you have to wear it until the clothes are broken, then they will only have to drink the northwest wind to live.

In the past, during the warlord era, those who held high positions and enjoyed high salaries mostly had tombstones without inscriptions. Cotton Market Remains Sluggish 194

The cotton market remains sluggish and trapped in a state of depression, mainly due to frequent adverse news. Although the American cotton market remained flat yesterday, the Indian cotton market experienced a sharp decline. Demand for local cotton is weak, while a large volume of Indian cotton has been traded. Although current various factors have not caused much impact, the future pressure may be difficult to avoid. It is reported that the recent sharp drop in American cotton prices has attracted the attention of cotton farmers, greatly reducing their interest in planting cotton, and there is a risk of a reduction in the new cotton planting area. If so, the American cotton market may gradually stabilize and provide impetus to the cotton market. However, the reduction in work by Indian yarn mills is also a hidden concern for the cotton market.

The futures cotton market continued to be sluggish. In the morning, the Exchange's Han Standard cotton was weaker due to the sharp drop in Indian cotton, with declines ranging from five fen to one qian for all months. The market remained weak in the afternoon, continuing to fall by five fen to one qian. However, the situation for the current month is quite varied. Statistics show that the total trading volume for the day was 21,400 dan. The closing prices of Han Standard cotton are recorded below: Han Standard Closing Price, Increase/Decrease, Account Balance; Closing Price, Increase/Decrease, Account Balance: 2 -- 35.05, down... 38,400; 5 -- 34.45, down 0... 67,700; 3 -- 34.60, 5... 65,000; 6 -- 34.55, down 15... 50,700; 4 -- 34.45, 5... 70,500; 7 -- 34.60, down 10... 29,700.

The sales of Indian cotton are strong again, while spot cotton transactions in the market remain weak. Indian cotton sales are strong again due to its low price. 200 bales arrived at the wharf. Transactions were as follows: Xing Heng Hua 35.00; Li Tai Factory purchased 300 pieces, to be shipped immediately, also 35.50; Yong An Factory purchased 3,000 pieces, 345 to be shipped; Oomra 34.50; Shen Xin Factory purchased 1,000 pieces, spot delivery to the factory; Wusong Hua 35.5 to 35.25, Pu Yi Factory purchased 400 bales, spot delivery to the factory; Da Cang Hua 36.25; Su Lun Factory purchased 200 bales, also delivered to the Su Factory.

Grain and Flour Market in Extreme Chaos 196

Yesterday, the flour market presented another chaotic situation. The ups and downs throughout the day were entirely driven by market sentiment. During the initial trading session in the morning, the current month once returned to 2 taels, 5 qian, 8 fen, and 7.5 li, which was one fen better than the closing price of the previous day. However, for the March contract, some factories continued to offer their positions, and short selling reappeared, resulting in strong selling pressure and an unstable market. During the second trading session, due to enthusiastic selling and the emergence of short positions, the current month's price fluctuated violently, with the closing price dropping to a low of 2 taels, 5 qian, 6 fen, and 2.5 li, which was a significant drop of 2.5 fen from the opening high. The other months were relatively calmer, falling by half a fen or seven li compared to the previous day. However, the situation changed again during the afternoon trading session. The months that had declined simultaneously in the morning now simultaneously turned upward because the quoted price of foreign wheat had slightly improved by two jiao or three to four jiao. Northern merchants were interested in the current month, so the opening was flat, but then it rose. The other months became stable because of this reason. Observing the subsequent situation, various factories have indeed ordered foreign wheat, so sharp increases should not be seen again in the future. As a result, the current month improved by 2.5 li compared to the previous day, March improved by 5 li, April remained unchanged, May improved by 7.5 li, June remained unchanged, and July decreased by 5 li.

Wheat Market Momentum Turns Slack 197

Yesterday, in the futures wheat market, the market situation for all months during the morning and afternoon sessions had become more moderate. Some outside speculators had already purchased a considerable amount a few days ago, but due to unfavorable opportunities and a sharp drop in the spot market, they inevitably had doubts. The buying interest in all months yesterday had come to a standstill, and the market value showed signs of softening. Observing the future trend, if there are further changes in foreign wheat prices, the market may still be unstable. As a result, the current month was down by 2 fen compared to the previous day, March and April were each down by 1 fen, and June and July new wheat were also each down by 1 fen. Spot wheat had no trading because factories mutually avoided it and had no intention of taking over.

Zhabei: Yesterday, the market was tight. Therefore, local merchants are holding firm and trying to raise prices. Top-quality japonica rice is priced at 19 yuan and 2 jiao, so most stores are focusing on medium and lower-grade goods. The need for silver dollars is earnest, so a turnaround may not be surprising.

Social News

The Question of Marriage Age by Zhuo Jun 205

The issue of marriage age is not just an important question within the context of marriage, but also a significant social and national issue, with connections to culture. Western countries have paid close attention to this issue for the past one hundred years or so. However, in China, there are still not many people who pay attention to this important question. According to a recent Japanese women's magazine, there is a growing trend for both men and women to marry later, and the driving force behind this trend is the increasing cost of living. Japan used to be known for its practice of early marriage, but now it seems that the custom of early marriage has been broken. In China, early marriage is still prevalent in some areas with less developed cultures. The drawbacks of early marriage are well known. For the sake of saving space, I won't go into detail. However, in marriage, the ages of the man and woman must be similar. If the man is much younger than the woman, or if the man is not yet developed while the woman is fully developed, there is a physiological need for correction.

According to Chen Xiao Xian's observations in Shanxi, in the early years of the Republic of China, Shanxi was characterized by marriages in which the ages of men and women were vastly different. He said that once he went to the countryside in Yuncheng and saw a strange situation: the bride was probably around twenty-one or two years old, while the groom was barely ten years old. Later, when he returned to Taiyuan, he asked several friends and learned that this custom was not only found in southern Shanxi, but also in northern Shanxi, such as Datong and Wutai. Chen also said that while this was the case in the early years of the Republic of China, he saw many similar situations when he returned to Shanxi in 1924.

According to Wang Hui Chuan, in the southeastern part of Anhui Province under the jurisdiction of She County, there is a place called Chang Biao Village. Boys as young as eleven or twelve years old often marry women, and the women they marry are at least eight or nine years older than them, or even ten years older. He also said that when the bride returns to her parents' home, the groom must accompany her. The bride's family hosts a banquet and always invites the groom to sit in the seat of honor. Because the groom is still wet behind the ears, he is the subject of many jokes. Sometimes, when he sees children outside the door throwing stones or playing kick shuttlecock, he doesn't realize that he is the groom and actually leaves his seat to play with the children outside.

The above two examples may be special cases. However, what a coincidence! I am afraid that this situation is not limited to Shanxi and Anhui. I dare not speculate whether this situation exists in other provinces. However, the fact that this situation still exists today suggests that it is not just a special phenomenon in Shanxi and Anhui. In any case, it is already wrong for boys of eleven or twelve years old to marry women, and it is especially wrong for them to marry women who are about ten years older than them. When we look at the marriage statistics from Massachusetts in the United States, we cannot find a report like the ones I mentioned above. In 1864, the average age of marriage in Massachusetts was 27 for men and 20.7 for women. In 1890, it was 27.2 for men and 24.4 for women. In 1895, it was 26.9 for men and 24.4 for women. In 1901, it was 27.3 for men and 24.6 for women. We cannot say whether their statistics are entirely reliable, but based on their statistics, we can believe that they absolutely do not allow men under the age of 20 to marry women. Also, based on their statistics, the age difference between men and women is generally only around four or five years. It is not impossible for women to marry men who are younger than them, but it is truly an obstacle to national health to have men who are not fully developed or underage marry women who are already developed or of age. If we were to say it humorously, wouldn't that be a joke?

It is true that in French marriage statistics, there are often cases where the age difference between men and women is around twenty years. However, this is because they marry later, and there is no phenomenon like what we see in Shanxi and Anhui. According to Berlin's 1906 marriage statistics, there were quite a few men around fifty-five years old and women around thirty-five years old. It turns out that it is a common phenomenon in modern times for the husband to be older than the wife. However, their statistics definitely do not include a situation where a man around ten years old marries a woman around twenty years old. When we look at the marriage statistics from Paris, France, we find that women who are older than their husbands make up less than 10% of the population, while couples who are the same age make up 3% to 4%. Looking at the marriage statistics from London, England, it can be seen that the majority of men who marry are over 25 years old, and the majority of women who marry are over 24 years old. It can be seen that it is a special phenomenon for men around ten years old to marry women.

Some say that in areas around the Indian subcontinent, both men and women marry around the age of eight or nine. This is common in India, but India is located in the tropics, and the climate is particularly warm. The development of both men and women is particularly fast. It is not uncommon for them to marry around the age of eight or nine. I am afraid that men around ten years old in China are not fully developed, and it seems that it is not physiologically appropriate for them to marry a fully developed woman.

There is one more point that must be mentioned in passing: the earliness or lateness of a man's or woman's marriage is related to their status in society. When they are in a certain position and it is not very good, their marriage age will be relatively earlier. On the contrary, when they are in a relatively higher position, their marriage age will often be higher. For example, miners and silk weavers in England generally marry around the age of twenty-four to twenty-six, and women generally marry around the age of twenty-two to twenty-four. Artists and shop assistants, on the other hand, must be thirty-six to twenty-eight years old before they are willing to marry, and women must be twenty-four to twenty-six years old before they are willing to marry. Lawyers and doctors, etc., who have a profession, generally do not marry until they are twenty-six to thirty years old, and women do not marry until they are twenty-six to twenty-eight or twenty-nine years old.

According to a recent Japanese correspondence in Life (Volume 5, Number 10), Japanese women generally do not marry until they are twenty-two or twenty-three years old, and men generally do not marry until they are twenty-six or twenty-seven years old. It can be seen that the marriage of men and women should follow physiological principles. In inland China, the patriarchal system still dominates. Fathers can't wait for their sons to marry early so that they can have grandsons as soon as possible, regardless of whether their sons are fully developed or whether the woman they marry their sons is too old and will affect or harm their sons' development.

Finally, I want to declare that this article has no system and makes no concrete contribution to the question of marriage age. However, this article aims to expose a special marriage situation in inland China and hopes that those who have the responsibility to guide and advise will think of a proper way to stop it.

Exhibition of Recent Works by Professors of the Chinese Academy of Art 206

Since its establishment, the Chinese Academy of Art has spared no effort in promoting art. As the spring semester is approaching and students from all over are gathering in Shanghai, in order to enhance the interest in research and promote the development of art, the school has specially organized an exhibition of recent works by professors at the school's second campus across from the Jiang Wan Road Park, starting on the 20th of this month, lasting for a week. The exhibition will feature works by Wang Dao Yuan, Guan Liang, Ni De Fang, Gan Min, Zhu Ying Peng, Tan Hua Mu, Zhang Da Qian, and Zeng Chao Kui, all of which are recent, carefully selected masterpieces. Their novel styles and outstanding expressiveness can be said to usher in a new era in the domestic art world.

Changes to Professors at Great China University 207

There have been slight changes to the professors at Great China University this semester. The former Dean of the College of Liberal Arts, Lu Xi Rong, and the Dean of the College of Education, Zhang Yao Xiang, have resigned from their positions due to their busy schedules, but have agreed to continue teaching a few courses. The University Affairs Council has approved the appointment of Wu Ze Lin, the former Director of the Preparatory Department, as the acting Dean of the College of Liberal Arts, and Chen Xuan Shan as the acting Dean of the College of Education. As for the Director of the Preparatory Department, Yu Zhi Han, the Director of the Preparatory Education Department, has been promoted. It is also learned that Zhang Zi Ping, who is admired by modern young people, will come to the school this semester to teach a course in primary school. (Recorded at the time)

Business News 208

The Great China Pharmacy is being organized. Xu Jing Gong, Wang Shi Peng, members of the executive committee of the Chinese National Legal Research Association, Liu Dao Ruo, director of general affairs at the Pingmin Hospital, and others have announced that they are launching the Great China Pharmacy, with a proposed capital of 500,000 yuan, specializing in Chinese and Western medicine and scientific equipment and materials. Its business scope will exceed that of all other pharmacies in this port, and it will be located on Zhejiang Road. 40% of the shares have been subscribed for domestically, and the remaining shares will be solicited from overseas Chinese. Liu is planning to travel to Singapore and the South Seas Islands on the 22nd of this month to raise funds for the Pingmin Hospital, while Xu and Wang will also travel together to solicit investments in Great China Pharmacy and to study foreign laws and various sciences. Their passports have been issued by the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, and they are scheduled to return to China in six months, at which time they will begin preparations for the opening of the pharmacy.

A clock and watch shop is being established in Xiaodongmen. Shi Xin Clock and Watch Shop has announced that recently, there have been many shops in the Xiaodongmen area, and the market is prosperous, but there is no well-established clock and watch shop. Now, watch expert Mr. Fan has established Shi Sheng Clock and Watch Shop on Jishui Street, Xiaodongmen Road, outside the city, to meet the needs of all sectors. It specializes in clocks, watches, eyeglasses, and German alarm clocks from famous factories in Europe, America, and Switzerland. It is fully equipped, and the facade has been renovated. Once the work is completed, a auspicious date will be chosen for the opening.

The Hongda Silk and Satin Store is scheduled to open soon. Hongda Silk and Satin Store, a newly opened shop in Xiaodongmen, has announced that since the completion of its new building, it has been purchasing famous silk and satin fabrics and decorating the interior. It is now well-prepared and will open on March 1st according to the Western calendar. At that time, it will sell all goods at reduced prices and offer gifts at half price.

The Liangchen Stationery Store amidst rising paper prices. Liangchen Good Friends Society at the intersection of Beijing Road and Zhejiang Road has announced that its Liangchen stationery is available in over a thousand types of drawings, and is also specialized in customized printing of stationery and envelopes. Paper prices have recently risen, but the store still sells stationery and envelopes at the old prices from eight years ago to ensure consistency. Dozens of samples of stationery and envelopes are available for selection, purchase, or custom printing. Those who request samples should include a one-jiao auxiliary coin for postage. Wholesale is particularly cheap.

Qingyise Restaurant's spring market. Qingyise Guangzhou Food Restaurant at the intersection of Sanma Road and Zhejiang Road has announced that since its opening, the restaurant has been crowded with diners, especially those holding spring banquets. The dishes have been specially improved, and the prices are very reasonable. The newly hired chef is sure to provide tasty flavors. Expert banquets, ranging from 12 yuan to over 100 yuan, can be booked in advance. Dishes can be delivered, and skilled chefs will be sent to the location to ensure satisfaction and avoid adding one, to show preferential treatment.

Theater News 210

The New Ailun Grand Theater Continues Showing "Beauty's Abduction": The New Ailun Grand Theater on Haining Road announces: Since this theater began showing domestically produced sound films with dialogue on New Year's Day, the theater has been packed every day, with extraordinary crowding. In order to cater to the public's psychology, the owner of this theater spared no expense in searching for famous domestic films to reward the elegant patronage. Furthermore, starting today, in response to requests from all sectors, this theater will specially continue showing "Beauty's Abduction" for two days, it is said.

Paris Theater Shows Naumen's Masterpiece Today: The Paris Grand Theater announces that it will begin showing the masterpiece of the great star Naumen Sila (Love Story of a Female Entertainer) starting today. This film is based on a famous stage play, with a convoluted plot, sensual and humorous, and unprecedented. In addition, Naumen's performance is delicate and more brilliant than in her previous films, it is said.

Social News Submission Guidelines 211

(1) Articles are limited to news about domestic and foreign science, industry, commerce, rural areas, health, aviation, exploration, customs, or urban life.

(2) Illustrations are limited to lyrical paintings of various aspects of social life.

(3) Photographs are acceptable if they are of seasonal scenery, landscapes, animals, plants, people, or related to news events. Seasonal landscape photography, especially with beautiful women, is welcome.

(4) Each article should not exceed 2,000 words.

(5) Do not write on both sides of the manuscript paper.

(6) Do not write the manuscript horizontally. The handwriting should be legible. Western text should be omitted where possible. If it is necessary to quote the original text, it must be attached below the Chinese text.

(7) Do not use blue ink to draw illustrations, and do not use colored paper. Use black ink on white paper.

(8) Address submissions to the Social News Department.

(9) Submitted manuscripts will not be returned, whether published or not. If you require a return, please state so in advance and include sufficient postage.

(10) Payment for articles is at the rate of three yuan, two yuan, or one yuan per thousand words. The same rate applies to each illustration or photograph. Special manuscripts will be paid separately.

Notice 212

(1) All businesses, film companies, theaters, calligraphers, painters, and doctors submitting manuscripts should indicate that they are addressed to the Shanghai Market Department.

(2) All businesses, film companies, theaters, calligraphers, painters, and doctors submitting manuscripts must affix a seal as proof of authenticity; otherwise, they will not be published.

(3) A small fee has traditionally been paid for lengthy film-related articles, as a mere embellishment. This practice remains in place, limited to one yuan per thousand words.
